  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bedda322-0bb8-47cf-a824-efeddedea674'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer6857695355581873269">My goodness, my memory is atrocious. I thought that the ending of this book was supposed to be the ending of the final book in the quartet, so now I will be continuing on with the series going in totally blind!<br/><br/>This was so enjoyable, I love these books so much. The nostalgia is real!<br/>I do think that they could have been fleshed out a little bit though. There is a bit of glossing over and jumping forward in time in big leaps, so things moved very fast in pace. I wish I had the chance to slow down a</span>
  <span id="freeText6857695355581873269" style="display:none">My goodness, my memory is atrocious. I thought that the ending of this book was supposed to be the ending of the final book in the quartet, so now I will be continuing on with the series going in totally blind!<br /><br />This was so enjoyable, I love these books so much. The nostalgia is real!<br />I do think that they could have been fleshed out a little bit though. There is a bit of glossing over and jumping forward in time in big leaps, so things moved very fast in pace. I wish I had the chance to slow down and savour it more.<br />Other than that, loved the action, the characters, the world.</span>

<div id="review_184344247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184344247" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2598584-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479388521p2/2598584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184344247?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/2598584-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442427648" href="/book/show/9821781-in-the-hand-of-the-goddess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184344247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13182157566919094476">I still enjoyed reading this series, but several more problems stood out more with this book. First off; important events kept being dropped casually into the conversation or mentioned in passing and that was that. I was very taken aback when it was said that Alanna's father died "last month", and that was about it. There were several other instances as well that this happened but I can't remember right now. Also time seems to be passing too quickly. At some point I had to struggle to keep up an</span>
  <span id="freeText13182157566919094476" style="display:none">I still enjoyed reading this series, but several more problems stood out more with this book. First off; important events kept being dropped casually into the conversation or mentioned in passing and that was that. I was very taken aback when it was said that Alanna's father died "last month", and that was about it. There were several other instances as well that this happened but I can't remember right now. Also time seems to be passing too quickly. At some point I had to struggle to keep up and remember that all these happened within long periods of time between each other. <br /><br />Then the romance. I appreciate that it's not overdramatized or anything, but I also felt like it... just happened. Like, in the last book there was no mention of it at all, and then suddenly in the first chapter of this book the goddess declared that George was in love with Alanna. That was jarring. So was when people suddenly started sleeping with each other without talking much about it at all. I was... confused. Some things that have had a huge build up (such as the Ordeal) ended up being too simple. I've noticed this pattern with pretty much all the climaxes in the series; they never even last more than a few pages. I mean, I hate reading about fighting/battles myself, but this is a book that's supposed to be all about it, right?<br /><br />Another gripe I have is that how Alanna seems to be a foolproof radar when it came to evil people. From the moment she saw Roger, she had already hated him inexplicably. Same with Delia, who turned out to be his pawn. I guess I really don't like it when evil people are so obviously portrayed to be evil from the start. There's no surprise, no twist, nothing. Wouldn't it have been more exciting if he seemed to be a good guy and then surprised by everyone by turning out not to be a good guy after all? Unreasonably "good instincts" in a hero is something I've always disliked.<br /><br />I don't know, maybe I'm just being picky. Or maybe this was meant for people much younger than me, hence the simplicity of the plot and everything. I could understand that, I guess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13182157566919094476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2108436954" />
    <a title="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as..........   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2108436954?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)" href="/user/show/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring">Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442427648" href="/book/show/9821781-in-the-hand-of-the-goddess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring?shelf=potential-to-go-big">potential-to-go-big</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring?shelf=what-the-fuck">what-the-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2108436954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12677419648721446676">Review and more at:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2018/01/19/in-the-hand-of-the-goddess-tamora-pierce/#more-5917'>https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress....</a><br/><br/>While I found this second book to have more thrills than the first book, I did feel there were things lacking here but only a little bit.<br/><br/>For starters I still think these books are way too short for what they are: high fantasy adventures. There’s no room for world building which is a shame because the world the author has created here has a lot of potential to be as intriguing and mysterious as Middle Earth. Here we get introduced to a go</span>
  <span id="freeText12677419648721446676" style="display:none">Review and more at:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2018/01/19/in-the-hand-of-the-goddess-tamora-pierce/#more-5917">https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress....</a><br /><br />While I found this second book to have more thrills than the first book, I did feel there were things lacking here but only a little bit.<br /><br />For starters I still think these books are way too short for what they are: high fantasy adventures. There’s no room for world building which is a shame because the world the author has created here has a lot of potential to be as intriguing and mysterious as Middle Earth. Here we get introduced to a goddess which we have no backstory on whatsoever and no hints on how the belief system in this world works. We also meet a purple eyed cat who is also special in the eyes of the goddess but we have no idea why. Will we find out in later books? I’m sure going to find out.<br /><br />In this book the time for our MC passes very quickly with her turning from young teenager to young adult in not many pages. Once again I will say I liked all the adventure and thrills these books have to offer as well as one of my favourite female characters in fantasy. Alanna herself remained to be as strong and brave as ever even when her secret was revealed in the end. Even though I saw that coming it still was handled in a very good manner with me wondering what will become of her in the next book.<br /><br />So in all this was still a good addition to a well crafted series, I just wish the books could be longer so there would be more room for world and character development as those have a lot of potential here.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12677419648721446676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_956248045" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956248045" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/956248045?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956248045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17051162528869177626">I was looking at the cover of my library copy of this book before I started it, and saw that on my edition, Alanna is pictured with a black cat on her shoulder. Remembering how delightfully full of wish fulfillment the first book was, I thought to myself, "Oh, she gets a cat in this one. I bet it's a magic cat. I bet it talks." I was joking. But I was totally right. Alanna not only acquires a talking cat (who also has purple eyes, natch), a deity swoops down to personally give Alanna a magic nec</span>
  <span id="freeText17051162528869177626" style="display:none">I was looking at the cover of my library copy of this book before I started it, and saw that on my edition, Alanna is pictured with a black cat on her shoulder. Remembering how delightfully full of wish fulfillment the first book was, I thought to myself, "Oh, she gets a cat in this one. I bet it's a magic cat. I bet it talks." I was joking. But I was totally right. Alanna not only acquires a talking cat (who also has purple eyes, natch), a deity swoops down to personally give Alanna a magic necklace. At this point, girlfriend is getting really weighted down with magical swag. She's going to have to start carrying trunks around with her, and I love it. <br /><br />The first book in the series moved quickly; <i>In the Hand of the Goddess</i> moves even faster, flying right through the rest of Alanna's training and ending soon after she graduates. This means that sometimes an entire year takes up only a few chapters, and the lengthy timeline means that the book can sometimes feel like just a string of separate events instead of a cohesive story. Halfway through the book, we get introduced to a neighboring country, Tusaine, and before we can even catch our breath, Alanna and her friends are being moved to the front lines because suddenly there's a war happening. I expected the war to take up a significant chunk of the story, because apparently I haven't grasped how this works yet, but instead the entire Tusaine conflict lasts about fifty pages before it's wrapped up and never really mentioned again. I had to finish the book and think back over the entire plot before I realized that the central story of this book is Alanna's continued struggle with Duke Roger, the evil sorcerer from Book One. I'm happy to report that by the end, Duke Roger <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[is out of the picture - Alanna kills him in a trial by combat, which also accomplishes the job of revealing her gender to everyone, which saves us some time - so he at least doesn't have to become a recurring villain who wears out his welcome <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The theme of this book is magic: not only do we have Alanna versus the evil sorcerer, but there's also a lot more about her own personal magic, and, as the title suggests, how the Goddess has specific plans for our heroine. Still not sure where we're going with all of this, but I'm confident that it will be awesome.<br /><br />The other important aspect of this book: in this installment, Alanna becomes sexually active, and I do not have enough space to fully explain how perfectly Tamora Pierce presents sex to her readers - the intended age group for these books, remember, is ten-to-twelve year olds. So there's this scene where Alanna decides that for fun she's going to put on a dress and walk around looking like a girl (there's a very subtle subplot in this book about Alanna learning that she can be a warrior <i>and</i> look like a girl, and that femininity does not equal weakness, and gaaaaahhhh I love it so much). For spoiler purposes I won't say which boy ends up putting the moves on her while she's in the dress, but for a minute it's kind of icky, because he's like, "You're fighting what has to be" and "Surely you've realized all along this had to happen" and I was thinking oh god, Tamora, please don't let our protagonist's first time happen after some boy emotionally coerces her into sex, but Alanna sticks to her guns and walks away. And THEN this crucial scene happens: Alanna is back in her room, and decides, on her own, that she's ready, and that she wants this, so <i>she</i> goes to <i>his</i> room and they have sex. It's so important that the sex is presented in exactly this way - as a choice that the girl makes because she wants it, not because anyone is pressuring her into it - and it's so subtly done that most girls in the target age group who read that scene won't even realize how important it is. And greatest of all, the sex isn't some great turning point in the story - it's just another part of growing up for Alanna, and isn't made out to be any more important than anything else that happens in the book. Little girls get so many messed up messages about sex growing up, and it's so great that Pierce's books tackle the subject so well, and this book gets an extra star because of it. <br /><br />In fact (and this relates to the previous point) the only place where this series still needs to improve is the way it treats female characters who are not Alanna. So far, Mistress Cooper is the only other female of substance, and in this book, we meet the first girl who is Alanna's age. Her name is Delia, she flirts with the boys and is generally the classic ultra-femme useless girl, and Alanna hates her. This is not great, and even worse, the girl <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[turns out to be a spy for Duke Roger. Hear that, little girls? If you see a girl flirting with a boy you like, it means she's evil <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. At this point in the series Alanna is totally that girl who says that she's "not like most girls" and only hangs out with guys because girls are so bitchy, and I <i>do not like it</i>. My hope for the next book: Alanna gets a female friend. And more magical swag. Maybe she'll get a dragon next.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17051162528869177626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1600032874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600032874" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600032874?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600032874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8155972631925516048"><b>Some girls have it easy. And they have it all</b>: <br/><br/>👉🏻 The love of a <b>Prince Charming</b> (for sure!). <br/>👉🏻 The love of an equally handsome <b>Prince of Thieves</b> (for the thrills!).<br/>👉🏻 <b>Good looks</b> that will explain points one and two (even if these good looks amount to red hair and purple eyes).<br/>👉🏻 Incredible <b>martial prowess</b> that allows one to defeat much larger and experienced opponents.<br/>👉🏻 <b>Strong magic</b>. Healing magic at that. <br/>👉🏻 But also a loving and devoted <b>brother who happens to be the strongest sorcerer</b> in liv</span>
  <span id="freeText8155972631925516048" style="display:none"><b>Some girls have it easy. And they have it all</b>: <br /><br />👉🏻 The love of a <b>Prince Charming</b> (for sure!). <br />👉🏻 The love of an equally handsome <b>Prince of Thieves</b> (for the thrills!).<br />👉🏻 <b>Good looks</b> that will explain points one and two (even if these good looks amount to red hair and purple eyes).<br />👉🏻 Incredible <b>martial prowess</b> that allows one to defeat much larger and experienced opponents.<br />👉🏻 <b>Strong magic</b>. Healing magic at that. <br />👉🏻 But also a loving and devoted <b>brother who happens to be the strongest sorcerer</b> in living memory. <br />👉🏻 And a <b>dedicated servant</b> who will take care of your fife remotely so that they do not have to be burdened with the mundane when saving the world. <br />👉🏻 <b>Magic sword</b>. A must. Really. <br />👉🏻 <b>Magic cat</b>. Also with purple eyes, for the record (honestly!).<br />👉🏻 And other <b>handy magic baubles</b>.<br />👉🏻 That come with <b>being the chosen one</b> of a Goddess. <br />👉🏻 Love and full <b>support of friends</b>.<br />👉🏻 As well as love and <b>support of a nearly every single person</b> they come across (except for the Sinister Antagonist or his Minions).<br />👉🏻 <b>Intelligence</b> bright enough to be the only person to identify and reveal the Sinister Antagonist and his machinations.<br /><br />Now, tell me <b>what can possibly be interesting about a story with such set up?</b> The first part of Alanna’s tale was interesting precisely because in order to become the first warrior maiden in hundreds of years, Alanna had to overcome several obstacles in herself (because she was a spoiled brat) and around her. And she did that with grace and humility that won me over. <br /><br />This book is written around the idea that <b>Alanna needs to conquer her three cardinal fears</b> to become a knight: a fear of love (see: points one and two), fear of the rite of passage that will take her to knighthood (see: points four and five), and her fear of the Sinister Antagonist (see: the rest). <b>It would be interesting if there would be anything challenging in these. Alas, there is not.</b> Everything that has been imperfect and this exciting about Alanna has long vanished (like the fact that she has been portrayed as not being a good empath, in this instalment her ability to feel people and situations in general is as flawless as the rest of her) and so she shines like a star regardless of the circumstances.<br /><br />Additionally, <b>the second wave feminism vibes</b> that were previously somewhat toned, go rampant here and the causal sex as well as the sexual emancipation is doubly jarring when compared with the middle-grade innocence of the last book. <br /><br />A definite, no thank you from me.<br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1509220933?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a> ★★★☆☆<br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600032879?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Woman Who Rides Like a Man</a> ★☆☆☆☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600032895?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lioness Rampant</a> ★☆☆☆☆</span>

<div id="review_264414400" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264414400" />
    <a title="Erica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2644090-erica"><img alt="Erica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558548351p2/2644090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264414400?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica" href="/user/show/2644090-erica">Erica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=flat-characters">flat-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=jf">jf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=growing-up">growing-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=women-and-girls">women-and-girls</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264414400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15075946542028384849">What happened??<br/><br/>I've read several of Tamora Pierce's books, but had not read the Song of the Lioness quartet and thought it time I start. I enjoyed the first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_' title='Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. I liked Alan, nee Alanna, in her single-minded determinedness and her unawareness of self and the effect she had on others. I liked the supporting characters. It was light, pleasant, and fun so I was eager to read this second book. I expected Alan to grow up and have to deal with identity issues, romantic i</span>
  <span id="freeText15075946542028384849" style="display:none">What happened??<br /><br />I've read several of Tamora Pierce's books, but had not read the Song of the Lioness quartet and thought it time I start. I enjoyed the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_" title="Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. I liked Alan, nee Alanna, in her single-minded determinedness and her unawareness of self and the effect she had on others. I liked the supporting characters. It was light, pleasant, and fun so I was eager to read this second book. I expected Alan to grow up and have to deal with identity issues, romantic issues and other problems that come with becoming a young adult. I expected the book to be less geared to 8-12 year-olds, as the first had been, and more written with teenagers in mind. These are the expectations I had before reading the boook. <br />I was terribly disappointed. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />While Alan <i>does</i> grow up and does have to deal with all the problems I had expected and while the book is <i>not</i> aimed at the 8-12 year-old set(though it's also not aimed at anyone over the age of 16), I felt the story to be tiresome and riddled with cliche. It was like reading a long-volumed shojo manga without the pictures in that the heroine is now a cute, determined girl whose existence is based on a lie, but those who know the truth love her even more because of her lie. Although she has very little sense of self and almost no discernable personality, she has a strong sense of right and duty and this is how she comes to all her decisions. She is also chosen of the Goddess, who even comes to visit the young heroine, bestowing gifts aplenty. She manages to snare the love of the two most eligible bachelors in the realm and has to choose between the two. In choosing, it's not so much that she makes an informed decision based on her feelings as she defaults to the one who is more available, falling into his bed out of convenience and because everyone keeps telling her she needs to learn to love. What about her makes her so endearing to all these men and one woman? <br /><br />Furthermore, everything she puts her hand to leads to success. She is instrumental in winning wars, she thwarts attempts made on her life without realizing they were attempts on her life. She is kidnapped but rescued before anything horrible can happen. And all the inconsistencies throughout the book are wrapped up tidily at the end: everyone was acting like an imbecile because there was a spell cast over them all, though there were moments of lucidity when one character or another would have suspicions. <br /><br />I loved Alan's determination and need to prove herself in the first book, when she was just out of childhood and was developing emotionally and physically. However, in this volume, it comes across as lack of awareness and the inability to react to her environment in a believable way. Instead, she relies mostly on luck, her steadfast friends, the Goddess and the writer's love of keeping her character safe. <br /><br />I was even more disappointed with the continuing villain who is supposedly the most powerful sorcerer around. He's slowly killing the queen, he has everyone under his control, he makes lame attempts on Alan's and Jonathan's lives and then he dies easily. So much for powerful sorcery. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I found myself rolling my eyes regularly at Alanna, her situations and the resolutions to all her problems. While many of the supporting characters remain interesting, they're not enough to carry the story. I am hoping this book was just a flimsy bridge to get to Alanna's adult life as a knight and I hope her further adventures prove to be more interesting and I hope she grows as a character, otherwise this is going to become a tedious series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15075946542028384849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13049350553379777387">I´m having a little hard time progressing with this book. In the first place, I chose this book because I was looking for a bad-ass female character and because of the good reviews. However, I´m having troubles liking Alanna. And the story itself. Why? Because in one chapter she is 13-year-old, in the next one, 15-year-old and so on. She starts being Jonathan´s lover when I´m still picturing her as a child, for God´s sake!<br/><br/>Another thing why don´t like her is because she keeps contradicting hersel</span>
  <span id="freeText13049350553379777387" style="display:none">I´m having a little hard time progressing with this book. In the first place, I chose this book because I was looking for a bad-ass female character and because of the good reviews. However, I´m having troubles liking Alanna. And the story itself. Why? Because in one chapter she is 13-year-old, in the next one, 15-year-old and so on. She starts being Jonathan´s lover when I´m still picturing her as a child, for God´s sake!<br /><br />Another thing why don´t like her is because she keeps contradicting herself. First, she says she never is going to love someone, bla, bla. Then, she becomes lover of Jonathan... and where does her pride go? And of course, I disagree with her choice. Jonathan over George?? WTF?<br /><br />EDIT: Well, I finally managed to finish the book. It was MEH. One of the things I don't understand is why everybody likes Alanna so much in the book? When she finally reveals she is a girl to all her friends (friends who were deceived for YEARS) they were like 'ok, we forgive you'. Just like that? No one was surprise, or angry or NOTHING! If this was a book for children it would be ok, but this is a YA book. The same with the rushness of the story, it happens all too fast.<br /><br />So, the first book was good and entertaining, the second... not so much. I have to think if I'm going to read the rest of the saga...</span>

<div id="review_134237550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134237550" />
    <a title="Fuchsia Rascal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/394650-fuchsia-rascal"><img alt="Fuchsia Rascal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359831216p2/394650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134237550?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuchsia Rascal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuchsia Rascal" href="/user/show/394650-fuchsia-rascal">Fuchsia Rascal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=political">political</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=women-writer">women-writer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=rereadin2012">rereadin2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=women-rock">women-rock</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134237550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9918782780871160622">5.0 nostalgia, 4.0 re-read, 4.5 actual.<br/><br/>Okay, I've re-read this many times, but never with as large a gap [3+ years] and as much a focus on critical thinking as now. That being said, although the Immortals Quartet stands as my favourite Tortall series and I relate to Diane more overall... this book has always been my favourite. And, looking at it critically, I stand by that judgment. It does have its faults [not all author-related], but its strengths make up for those. I do have a couple of discl</span>
  <span id="freeText9918782780871160622" style="display:none">5.0 nostalgia, 4.0 re-read, 4.5 actual.<br /><br />Okay, I've re-read this many times, but never with as large a gap [3+ years] and as much a focus on critical thinking as now. That being said, although the Immortals Quartet stands as my favourite Tortall series and I relate to Diane more overall... this book has always been my favourite. And, looking at it critically, I stand by that judgment. It does have its faults [not all author-related], but its strengths make up for those. I do have a couple of disclaimers for people who are reading it in their post-teen years: this book is decidedly in a market of its time. The entire series' length was cut in half, at <i>least</i>, due to publishers not believing that a fantasy novel, especially with a female protagonist, would sell well in the years before Harry Potter [author Tamora Pierce has commented on this numerous times throughout the past 15 years]. As a result, the characters, plot, and novelization are rushed throughout the first two books [which, combined, take place over 8 years], which gives the books a juvenile feel. This is a result of publishing [oh, how I wish I could read those original versions of the first two books!] and something that's not reflected in Tammy's later novels, whether the last two books of this series or subsequent series. If you can get past the juvenile-esque writing of these first two books, you will be duly rewarded, I assure you.<br /><br />I can't tap into what originally made me declare this book my favourite book of all time. I originally read these books in 1996, pre-Protector of the Small quartet and actually, pre-most-of-the-Immortals-quartet. I identified with Alanna's need to get out and prove herself against ~masculine~ warriors. I came into this series obsessed with Joan of Arc, but already familiar with the world [and slightly with Alanna's legacy] via <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/546113.Wild_Magic__Immortals___1_" title="Wild Magic (Immortals, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Wild Magic</a>. I left this series as a feminist activist, thankful that Alanna was a character who presented both masculine and feminine qualities. But, admittedly, I've evolved beyond my 13 year old definitions of feminism in the last 15 years since I originally read this book. All that being said, it's still my favourite.<br /><br />The strong point of this novel is, in my opinion, Alanna's acceptance of her gender. You might disagree with that but, in my perception, that is what hit strongest. In this book, Alanna becomes more <i>real</i>, fighting her desire for love vs. her knowledge of the pain it causes; her feminine side vs. the masculine side that will keep her safe. She has chosen a masculine identity [until her knighting] that will keep her free and safe from harassment and yet, despite this, she explores what it means to be a female and what it will mean after she's earned her shield. She's an excellent student and squire but that doesn't mean that she knows everything, something she learns fairly quickly during her squire training.<br /><br />Personally, the steps Alanna takes towards accepting her femininity mean the world to me. At this point, I don't really care about her knight training or her relationship between Jonathan or George. Alanna taught me how to accept both femininity and masculinity, and accept what they meant to <i>me</i>. I can't put a rating on that. What matters is that it made me think about it and come to my own conclusions. What makes a female a female? What makes up masculine characteristics? Alanna shows that you can be a bit of both, honestly.<br /><br />So many feels, y'all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9918782780871160622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13533024082021976797"><i>"Roger's suite of rooms was located very conveniently for Alanna's purposes."</i><br/><br/><b>This entire book was damned convenient for her!!!</b><br/><br/>I thought the first book was alright and picked this up because the entirety of tumblr was shitting themselves over the feminist shit in this book. Let me tell you, there was some shit in this. And were they feminist? <br/><br/>Alanna doesn't want love but because the author deemed it must happen, she's aged up 6 years in only a few chapters. And the creeps trickle in....<br/><br/>Alanna has</span>
  <span id="freeText13533024082021976797" style="display:none"><i>"Roger's suite of rooms was located very conveniently for Alanna's purposes."</i><br><br><b>This entire book was damned convenient for her!!!</b><br><br>I thought the first book was alright and picked this up because the entirety of tumblr was shitting themselves over the feminist shit in this book. Let me tell you, there was some shit in this. And were they feminist? <br><br>Alanna doesn't want love but because the author deemed it must happen, she's aged up 6 years in only a few chapters. And the creeps trickle in....<br><br>Alanna has 2 love interests. Jon the prince who's sleeping with several women at court and the King of Thieves, George. At first I was all F Yeah Princes! but then this happened:<br><br><i>"It's a charm to-keep me from having children," she stammered. "Mistress Cooper gave it to me a-a long time ago."<br>Jon chuckled. "Have you ever tried it out?" he asked."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479273493ra/21167417.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>"What's that supposed to mean?" she asked gruffly.<br>"This." Swiftly he kissed her again and again. Alanna felt giddy and was grateful that his tight hold kept her from falling. <b>She was scared.</b> She suddenly realized she wanted to be the one in his bed tonight."</i><br><br>....ok, that's cool, BUT.<br><br><i>Jonathan stopped kissing her, only to start unlacing her bodice. <br>Alanna shoved him away, teffired. "No!" she gasped, grabbing her laces. "I was crazy to think-Johanathan, please!"</i><br><br>So he stops and throws this line:<br><br><b>"You're fighting what has to be, he said, "and you know it as well as I do."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479273493ra/21167418.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But because the author just wanted the romance to happen, Alanna gives in to his pestering and sleeps with him. WTF. Such feminism. Much girl power. Wow.<br><br>Then we have George, who is much better than Jon, but also has creepy moments of his own, thus making him another creeper and another reason to be disappointed. These include forcing a kiss on her when she can't resist him and drugging her because she needs to rest.<br><br>Gee, thanks for considering Alanna's feelings on the matter.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479273493ra/21167419.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>These weren't even the tip of the iceberg! <br><br>You wondered what would happen if her secret of being a woman got out? Ha!! It's utterly ridiculous.<br><br>You wondered what the final showdown with Roger would be like? LOL even the most powerful sorcerer in the world is no match for Alanna. Who's only 16.<br><br>Just no.<br><br>While I admire Pierce's desire to write a series featuring a powerful heroine for women, I can't say that the events of this book supported her views. I admire what she wanted to write, but what this book became was not that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13533024082021976797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_768294913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/768294913" />
    <a title="Gianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14536303-gianna"><img alt="Gianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352789664p2/14536303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/768294913?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gianna" href="/user/show/14536303-gianna">Gianna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer768294913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7570024958743066252">I'm pretty sure "Tamora Pierce" is just the pen name of a precocious child, because this series reads like it was written by and for 12-year-old girls. Let's start with the names: Moonlight, Darkness, Lightning, and Faithful. Really? <br/>Then let's get to plot. Things don't happen naturally, they just occur because the author wants them to. All of a sudden men start falling in love with Alanna for no apparent reason. Alanna will never get distracted by love, but then someone kisses her and she hops </span>
  <span id="freeText7570024958743066252" style="display:none">I'm pretty sure "Tamora Pierce" is just the pen name of a precocious child, because this series reads like it was written by and for 12-year-old girls. Let's start with the names: Moonlight, Darkness, Lightning, and Faithful. Really? <br />Then let's get to plot. Things don't happen naturally, they just occur because the author wants them to. All of a sudden men start falling in love with Alanna for no apparent reason. Alanna will never get distracted by love, but then someone kisses her and she hops right into bed. Anything bad that happens is resolved instantly; there is no danger and no consequences. <br />Other bothersome things: The Duke Roger situation. Alanna goes into his chambers to gather evidence, and then says she can't believe she never suspected him. But she did suspect him! The entire time! From the first moment she met him! <br />The knighthood ordeal. Spiders and being cold? Sounds super hard. The stuff of legends, truly. <br />Racism. All the characters are white except for a mystical, magical Asian monk who is described as "yellow." In the audiobook he even speaks with an accent. Way to stereotype. <br />I started this series because I loved the premise, but I can't take any more. I wouldn't even recommend it to young readers who might not be as easily irritated as I am, because Alanna's romantic relationships are unhealthy, bordering on abuse. George (how old is he anyway? 40?) kisses her when her hands are too full to stop him. I expected her to put a knife to his throat, but she's totally fine with it. I don't think we should be teaching girls that men forcing affection is romantic in any way. Jonathan is super jealous and demanding and makes her do stuff she doesn't want to do. Once again, I expect her to put him in his place, but she does whatever he tells her and doesn't confront him for being a crappy boyfriend. <br />I only finished this book because it was short and I wanted to be able to write a well-informed bad review. Don't bother with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7570024958743066252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3055529529" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3055529529" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16092014-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422940350p2/16092014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3055529529?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/16092014-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780689310546" href="/book/show/1103191.In_the_Hand_of_the_Goddess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16092014-paul?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16092014-paul?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16092014-paul?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3055529529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1933027373610279270">It took me too long to finally return to the Song of the Lioness series, which opened with the excellent <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_' title='Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. But I'm glad I did, and now that I've refreshed my memory with how fun and easy to read these middle-school-to-YA fantasy novels are, I'll probably just power through and finish them.<br/><br/>In the first book, we're introduced to Alanna, who disguises herself as a boy to fulfill her dream of becoming a knight. She makes great friends, fights baddies, and manages to keep h</span>
  <span id="freeText1933027373610279270" style="display:none">It took me too long to finally return to the Song of the Lioness series, which opened with the excellent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_" title="Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. But I'm glad I did, and now that I've refreshed my memory with how fun and easy to read these middle-school-to-YA fantasy novels are, I'll probably just power through and finish them.<br /><br />In the first book, we're introduced to Alanna, who disguises herself as a boy to fulfill her dream of becoming a knight. She makes great friends, fights baddies, and manages to keep her secret for the most part. As you might expect, the second book is more of the same, only somewhat more episodic as the action stretches over several years. As with many stories relying on a semi-magical world, the <i>deuses ex machina</i> proliferate to ensure our heroine is never in any danger she can't scrape her way out of.<br /><br />It's pretty easy to pick this story apart, but that would be pretty curmudgeonly; this is a <i>fun</i> series, and certainly more worth reading than, say, Marion Zimmer Bradley's similarly feminist-inflected fantasy for adults, which is weighed down with its own sense of self-importance and our knowledge of the author's horribleness. <br /><br />I'd recommend this pretty highly for readers age 10+.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1933027373610279270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3055529529">
  <td colspan="2">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer41348500" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16319448081129274260"><br/><b>Re-read January</b><br/><br/>I think this might be my least favorite Alanna, at least on this read. I got bored with the battle and for all the revelations at the end to happen!<br/><br/>I like past me's comments about the love triangle. I've read more bad ones recently, and still like this one.<br/><br/><b>Original Review</b><br/><br/>So, of course I've read this many times before and I was enjoying the book, but going a bit slowly and then I reached about the halfway point and read it straight though!   <span id="freeText16319448081129274260" style="display:none"><br /><b>Re-read January</b><br /><br />I think this might be my least favorite Alanna, at least on this read. I got bored with the battle and for all the revelations at the end to happen!<br /><br />I like past me's comments about the love triangle. I've read more bad ones recently, and still like this one.<br /><br /><b>Original Review</b><br /><br />So, of course I've read this many times before and I was enjoying the book, but going a bit slowly and then I reached about the halfway point and read it straight though! I think I always have a bit of a harder time with younger protagonists, so I like the books better when Alanna gets a little older.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Alanna's deepening relationships with both George and Jon. I've been complaining recently about love triangles in current popular YA and maybe the biggest reason I started this re-read is because I think it's done so well here. Neither boy pushes Alanna into anything. Alanna doesn't just <i>say</i> she has bigger priorities than love, she actually follows through on it. And she loves, but she's still unsure about what it all means. That's just so real to me.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780739330494" href="/book/show/6764160-in-the-hand-of-the-goddess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3161638277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16465776262884793605">After a strong start to this series, this book is a slight step back. We continue to follow Alan/Alana as she gets ready to take the tests for her knighthood, and we continue with uncovering the plot kill the king and prince. Plus, Alana gets a talking cat courtesy of the goddess.<br/><br/>You know, on top of the violet eyes, the sword she King Arthur'd out of the cellar, and the amulet, her healing abilities and now her magical cat, I'm starting to suspect that Alana just might be Special. At least she's</span>
  <span id="freeText16465776262884793605" style="display:none">After a strong start to this series, this book is a slight step back. We continue to follow Alan/Alana as she gets ready to take the tests for her knighthood, and we continue with uncovering the plot kill the king and prince. Plus, Alana gets a talking cat courtesy of the goddess.<br /><br />You know, on top of the violet eyes, the sword she King Arthur'd out of the cellar, and the amulet, her healing abilities and now her magical cat, I'm starting to suspect that Alana just might be Special. At least she's not entirely a Mary Sue. A couple of characters hate her (the evil ones, of course) and she doesn't do everything perfect the first time, but it's a near thing. Oh, and of course, she's got two different guys interested in her, because of course she does. And of course, both men are gross about it in their own special ways. *rolls eyes* <br /><br />While still competently written, this suffers a little from lack of plot. It felt more like several subplots strung together between the bindings of a book. It was interesting to see Alana learning how to be a girl again after all these years spent being a boy, and I did love the cat. How could I not? But this felt more like filler, and I think it resolved the assassination plot much too neatly and tidily.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16465776262884793605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_788438385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/788438385" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/888230-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369409361p2/888230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/788438385?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/888230-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer788438385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10099693987512430506">Where do I start? <br/>These books came with such high reviews, and I was really excited to start reading it. But then I started reading it. First off, Alanna is a Mary Sue. Anything that happens ends perfectly, with no consequences to the characters. She's stereotypical and isn't consistent at all. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ She says she doesn't want to fall in love, yet she's suddenly in Jonathan's bed and the author tells us she's his lover, with no build-up or introduction to that twist at all.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoil</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText10099693987512430506" style="display:none">Where do I start? <br />These books came with such high reviews, and I was really excited to start reading it. But then I started reading it. First off, Alanna is a Mary Sue. Anything that happens ends perfectly, with no consequences to the characters. She's stereotypical and isn't consistent at all. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She says she doesn't want to fall in love, yet she's suddenly in Jonathan's bed and the author tells us she's his lover, with no build-up or introduction to that twist at all.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Meanwhile, the years progress between pages, and months can pass by between paragraphs leaving the reader totally lost and annoyed. Things that are supposedly major plot-points have no build-up and end within a few pages, with no reflection.<br />I secretly believe that this book was written by a 12-year old girl as names like 'Moonlight', and 'Faithful' litter the pages. The author never addresses any real struggles that a girl acting as a boy would face, does nobody really notice that her voice hasn't changed, or that she has no facial hair? Really?<br /><br />There's so much more I could say about this book and how disappointed I am with it. It was painful to finish. I think my brain is bleeding.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10099693987512430506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78004687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78004687" />
    <a title="kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2125614-kris"><img alt="kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325962640p2/2125614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78004687?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kris" href="/user/show/2125614-kris">kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78004687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12240183561944555750">[first read 3 January 2008; 4 stars]<br/><br/> Speeding through years of Alanna's squirehood, her Ordeal, and a final showdown with Duke Roger the Evil Sorcerer, <i>In the Hand of the Goddess</i> wraps up Alanna's quest to become a knight with more of a whimper than a bang. We leave our faithful Lady Knight preparing to depart for the south on adventures of her own (which I am PUMPED FOR). <br/><br/>1. Alanna's secret is pretty much not hers to share, huh? She doesn't get to reveal it to the king and queen and the rest of</span>
  <span id="freeText12240183561944555750" style="display:none">[first read 3 January 2008; 4 stars]<br /><br /> Speeding through years of Alanna's squirehood, her Ordeal, and a final showdown with Duke Roger the Evil Sorcerer, <i>In the Hand of the Goddess</i> wraps up Alanna's quest to become a knight with more of a whimper than a bang. We leave our faithful Lady Knight preparing to depart for the south on adventures of her own (which I am PUMPED FOR). <br /><br />1. Alanna's secret is pretty much not hers to share, huh? She doesn't get to reveal it to the king and queen and the rest of the court on her terms; she didn't get to tell Jonathan on her terms: all together, her agency is kind of run roughshod over which is distasteful to me. <br /><br />2. On that note: can someone please tell me why Gary is the one who she tells her secret to (mostly, it seems, because Jonathan picks him for her?)? This right here is exactly what I meant about Alanna's selfishness: is there any difference between Gary and Raoul (at <i>this</i> stage of the story? Yes, there is further development in later books, but <i>here</i>, <i>now</i>, facing her Ordeal: why does she pick Gary? What sets him apart from the rest of the hoard?)?<br /><br />3. lskdjfldjk JONATHAN. I wished I liked this story arc more: what I wouldn't give for a heroine to have a romance that doesn't end in HEA but remains a healthy, loving relationship instead of a "learning opportunity" for her future hero (UGH). Except I DIDN'T LIKE THIS RELATIONSHIP AT ALL. <br /><br />Part of it is the fact that it develops when Alanna is still serving as Jonathan's squire? And Alanna makes several comments about how her life is his—not because she loves him in a romantic sense, but because she is his liege. And her examination of why she wants to be his lover is rooted in jealousy and half-dismissed out of her own fear (which she does acknowledge!)—but it doesn't ever crack a surface-level. It's extraordinarily shallow, and <i>easy</i> and instead of feeling like she's <i>choosing</i> to be with Jonathan in a romantic sense, it rather feels like he's available (connecting rooms!), he's down with it (he's flirting with all the ladies), and she's curious (although she tries very hard to stop that train of thought). <br /><br />This ties into the above: that the Alanna series does not do its relationships justice. They are simple, easy things: if Alanna likes a person, they are good. If Alanna does not like a person, they are evil. Taking a lover is an easy decision (once the decision has been made). There are no complexities to the people Alanna interacts with: they are either for her, or against her, or tools for her to learn her lesson (i.e., the lesson to "love" as given to her by the Goddess). I found myself flinching away from Alanna far more than I recall, wanting there to be a deeper examination of her life, her world, her actions, her peers, her masters.<br /><br />4. In the vein of THAT RELATIONSHIP, up until she makes the decision to open her door for him, all the physical manifestations of attraction are done <i>to</i> Alanna: she is kissed several times without her permission. She is hugged. She is touched. She does not instigate any of it, which makes her decision to take Jon as her lover seem all the more like it came out of nowhere??? (George is guilty of the kissing, too! HOW COULD YOU GEORGE.)<br /><br />ALSO, when Alanna is describing Jonathan's tantrums (which, I believe, are supposed to read as the angsty fits of a love-lorn suitor???), they read as dangerous and manipulative. She has to flirt with ladies and can't talk to boys and has to look a certain way and has to dance with the people Jonathan says she has to dance with and and and!! THIS IS NOT COOL BEHAVIOR.<br /><br />I remain squicked out by the relationship. <br /><br />5. AHAHA STUPID ROGER. <br /><br />6. OH THOM. <br /><br />SORRY I HAD A THOUGHT: I think I recall from an interview with Pierce several years ago that the Alanna Quartet was originally meant to be one novel but publishers at the time did not believe that a larger book would sell and so she was asked to break her original manuscript into pieces. From my current vantage point mid-arc, I'm curious what sort of impact that tidbit has on the flow of things.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12240183561944555750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16486731219375563510">I think this is the book I forgot the most of. In fact, I remembered almost none of it, with the exception of Faithful. I remembered Faithful. It would also explain how I managed to conflate books one and two. I remembered next to nothing about book 2, except Alanna getting a cat, starting to wear women's clothing sometimes, and <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[sleeping with Jonathan <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.   <span id="freeText16486731219375563510" style="display:none">I think this is the book I forgot the most of. In fact, I remembered almost none of it, with the exception of Faithful. I remembered Faithful. It would also explain how I managed to conflate books one and two. I remembered next to nothing about book 2, except Alanna getting a cat, starting to wear women's clothing sometimes, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[sleeping with Jonathan <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The first two, I thought happened in book one, the third in book three.<br /><br />This is a good book, and I like it as part of the Alanna series, but it's not as good as the first one for me. For one, I forgot how much time it covers, and how quickly that time moves. First there's the potential for a war, then all of a sudden it's a year later and they're at war, then it's another year or two and Alanna's facing her Ordeal. And then it's the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also thought the final dispatching of Roger was a little quickly wrapped up. Alanna just breaks into his room and finds the proof she needs. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As for the Chamber of the Ordeal, I wish there'd been a way for Tamora Pierce to be vaguer on the details. The Chamber is scary because you don't know what's so terrible. I feel like it's hard for a concrete reality to live up to that kind of fear.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also really wish Alanna had gotten to announce that she was a girl on her own terms <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'm also not super into how the relationship with Jonathan develops. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Particularly when he tells her they're essentially inevitable as a couple. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I continue to like how Alanna's relationship with George is treated. I fee like he understands her better.<br /><br />And lastly, I wish we'd gotten to see more of some of the relationships that are so wonderfully described in the first book. I wanted more Alanna and Myles and Alanna and Gary (instead of just Alanna and her love interests). Also, a female friend wouldn't have gone amiss. I aso woul have liked to see a little more of the aftermath of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Duke Roger's death (the snake) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Particularly with regards to some of the stuff with Alex, and how he was affected.<br /><br />For me good, not spectacular. Not the first one.<br /><br />2016 Reading Challenge: A book you can read in less than a day.</span>

<div id="review_111282193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111282193" />
    <a title="Ravyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3453660-ravyn"><img alt="Ravyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269311674p2/3453660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111282193?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ravyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ravyn" href="/user/show/3453660-ravyn">Ravyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3453660-ravyn?shelf=z-young-adult">z-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111282193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7745398931604890189">Even though I didn't exactly fall in love with the first novel of this series, I just couldn't help myself from wanting to find out what would happen with Alanna. Would her secret be revealed? Would she fall in love? Would she finally face her arch nemesis, Roger?<br/><br/>Well, you'll just have to read book 2 to find out, won't you? <br/><br/>Unfortunately, I found book 2 to be plagued with many of the same issues that bothered me about book 1. For starters, it felt like many of the details or key scenes were glos</span>
  <span id="freeText7745398931604890189" style="display:none">Even though I didn't exactly fall in love with the first novel of this series, I just couldn't help myself from wanting to find out what would happen with Alanna. Would her secret be revealed? Would she fall in love? Would she finally face her arch nemesis, Roger?<br /><br />Well, you'll just have to read book 2 to find out, won't you? <br /><br />Unfortunately, I found book 2 to be plagued with many of the same issues that bothered me about book 1. For starters, it felt like many of the details or key scenes were glossed over or simply mentioned in passing instead of actually being played out in the story. The timeline skips ahead by leaps and bounds, and not always in a very clear manner. All in all, it just felt like there was a much greater, longer story to be told, but that it had been cut down to the bare minimum or had never been developed at all so as to be shorter in length. For example, I found myself incredibly frustrated by the so called "romantic" developments within the novel, as this was pretty much glossed over and reduced to a mere handful of sentences. I just would have liked to see more -- more romance, more explanation, more magic, more story development and detail in general.<br /><br />Although I'm glad to have continued this series in order to find out some of Alanna's fate, I'm not sure that I will be reading any further. With the advent of so many "young adult" books written for an adult audience as well, I realize that I may have had different expectations for this book than what it deserved. Ultimately, I think that this series does have its merits, but at the end of the day, I believe it is much better suited for enjoyment by its intended audience: older children and young adults.<br /><br /><b>Bottom Line:</b> Probably would be enjoyed most by young girls. At least, I'm pretty sure I would have liked it a lot more when I was 12 or so.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7745398931604890189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
