<div id="review_3158577376" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3158577376" />
    <a title="steph // bookplaits" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37929038-steph-bookplaits"><img alt="steph // bookplaits" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577746310p2/37929038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3158577376?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="steph // bookplaits" class="user" itemprop="url" name="steph // bookplaits" href="/user/show/37929038-steph-bookplaits">steph // bookplaits</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8248438-in-the-hand-of-the-goddess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37929038-steph-bookplaits?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3158577376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer608860547955588853">There have definitely been times where I’ve come to love a series as I read the sequels, but usually what happens is that I rate the first book 3 stars (sometimes 2 stars!) and the ratings then go up from there. So, the fact that I rated the second book in the Song of the Lioness quartet worse than the first one isn’t a great sign! I *think* I still want to continue the readalong because I’m definitely curious about Pierce’s later series and I don’t want to read those without having read the Ala</span>
  <span id="freeText608860547955588853" style="display:none">There have definitely been times where I’ve come to love a series as I read the sequels, but usually what happens is that I rate the first book 3 stars (sometimes 2 stars!) and the ratings then go up from there. So, the fact that I rated the second book in the Song of the Lioness quartet worse than the first one isn’t a great sign! I *think* I still want to continue the readalong because I’m definitely curious about Pierce’s later series and I don’t want to read those without having read the Alanna books. Or at least spoilery summaries of them, I suppose... 🤔<br /><br />Although I do like Alanna (and really liked the addition of Faithful! 😻) there were a few things in this story that didn’t work well for me.<br /><br />First, I like the *sound* of Alanna’s friendship group, but they didn’t seem to get much page time, so I didn’t feel like I got to *know* them. They were just kind of... there in the background.<br /><br />Second, I struggled with the amount of time covered. For such a short book (&lt;300 pages!), quite a few years pass, and it’s a little disorienting at points because not a lot of time is given to this; the story just jumps ahead.<br /><br />Third, although the story was easy to read and there were a few scenes that made me smile, I didn’t get any sense of urgency from the war or the various fight scenes. The target audience of this series isn’t adult, so I guess this factor makes sense, but overall the story felt a bit... directionless. 🤔 I just wasn’t sure what the point of everything was!<br /><br />On a final note, one thing that bothered me was the description of a man as ‘yellow’. I initially thought I’d misread that as the colour of his clothes and went back to check, but nope... it seems to be a description of his skin colour. I assume Pierce’s writing is a lot better in her more recent work though. This series is quite old, after all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="608860547955588853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3158577376">
  <td colspan="2">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer651052207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4930603118064168510">Rating: 2 Stars/DNF<br/><br/>It seems as if Tamora Pierce and I must part our ways. Quite simply put, I am above the age group to enjoy this. While I know many of my older friends have loved this, I seem to have lost interest in the life and struggles of a mere fifteen-year-old girl, which says everything about me and nothing about the book itself. I've only ever read The Immortals Series by Pierce when I was ten and I suspect I'd have loved this as much, if not more, if I were the same age. Alas, Alanna </span>
  <span id="freeText4930603118064168510" style="display:none">Rating: 2 Stars/DNF<br /><br />It seems as if Tamora Pierce and I must part our ways. Quite simply put, I am above the age group to enjoy this. While I know many of my older friends have loved this, I seem to have lost interest in the life and struggles of a mere fifteen-year-old girl, which says everything about me and nothing about the book itself. I've only ever read The Immortals Series by Pierce when I was ten and I suspect I'd have loved this as much, if not more, if I were the same age. Alas, Alanna fails to capture my attention and although this novel is written impeccably with thoughtful musings and a solid plot line, I'd only recommend it to younger readers or readers who enjoy intelligent literature for younger YA. As I grow I seem to prefer my protagonists to be older and can't seem to wait for Alanna to grow up. Sadly, this is just a classic case of it's-me-not-you syndrome.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1510667175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510667175" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510667175?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=project-nostalgia">project-nostalgia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510667175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16203915280149080730">More notes!<br/><br/>On the Ordeal: Alanna describes Jonathan coming out of the Chamber - <blockquote>In her mind she saw Jonathan stumble out of that iron-barreled Ordeal Chamber, his face gray. He had looked at her without seeing her - Jonathan! Sometimes even now his eyes went dark and blank, and she knew that he was remembering the Ordeal. Her voice shook as she said, "He looked like some part of him <i>died</i> in there..."</blockquote>Then, later, when Jonathan and Gary are about to instruct Alanna in her Ordeal, they both mention</span>
  <span id="freeText16203915280149080730" style="display:none">More notes!<br /><br />On the Ordeal: Alanna describes Jonathan coming out of the Chamber - <blockquote>In her mind she saw Jonathan stumble out of that iron-barreled Ordeal Chamber, his face gray. He had looked at her without seeing her - Jonathan! Sometimes even now his eyes went dark and blank, and she knew that he was remembering the Ordeal. Her voice shook as she said, "He looked like some part of him <i>died</i> in there..."</blockquote>Then, later, when Jonathan and Gary are about to instruct Alanna in her Ordeal, they both mention barely surviving the Ordeal. I keep thinking these descriptions don't quite match the Ordeals Alanna and Kel go through. There's a lot more background I want. First: who made this thing? How does it keep running? Why did Duke Gareth lose his finger if the rest of them get living nightmares? What's the purpose of the living nightmares? Who decided that they're not allowed to talk about the Ordeal after it's over, or scream while it's happening?<br /><br />Anyway. On the actual story: <br /><br />I always loved Alanna dueling that knight from Tusaine. The dialogue is perfect. Jonathan taunting the knight with his squire, Alanna saying she didn't kill him because he was stupid, and "If I killed everyone who was stupid, I wouldn't have time to sleep." <br /><br />And then, of course, they go to war with Tusaine. You know, I get a big kick out of the whole war - it goes by in so few pages, and the resolution is really great and unexpected - but I have a bunch of questions this time around. Why does it take so long for people to reach obvious conclusions in this series? Or are the conclusions only obvious because Pierce telegraphs them in her writing, and I'm being unreasonable expecting so much from the characters? For example, only Alanna thinks of going to Stephan about the burr in Duke Gareth's saddle? No one, not even the Lord Provost, notices that there have been TWO recent sicknesses healers can't battle, and that the line of succession contains one of the few sorcerers capable of brewing up a disease like that? Seriously? Why does Miles only question Duke Roger's assignment for Jonathan quietly, without reading some of Roger's ambitions in the action? Isn't Miles supposed to be a) a smart guy and b) the king's spymaster? Or is he only Jonathan's spymaster, and I'm mixing up the chronology? <br /><br />There are references later to Roger's spell, but - I mean - how long has he had them in that mesh spellbag thing? So long? <br /><br />Delia of Eldorne. She's kind of a stereotype, but it works here. I think. I do like Pierce's careful POV changes, and that we got to see her interacting with Roger. <br /><br />I also think Roger is a fabulous sneaky villain. <br /><br />ANOTHER GOOD ONE. This is a great series. I question it so much because it's so real that I want to resolve any inconsistencies threatening that worldbuilding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16203915280149080730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wobjb57Mqfp+i2XBcgyk6gr82ru/IOa4tBv2+phKFNinWQiw95LZDjgA/bXfxuQ77fMMgOY2jBJTizonvqIWIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mkrGcCTpCPVbFBjkpqGjSQaWLgoX7j9ckx+HySh9saH/lS2vTbd4AR2fgJALa+OY4Zn4MU74VfZ0j0sUDpWzWA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10425979814596551807">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br/><br/>I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br/>Though I would love to join gro</span>
  <span id="freeText10425979814596551807" style="display:none">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br /><br />I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br />Though I would love to join groups, I'm going to turn them all down. I just don't have the time to take part, so please don't be offended if I don't join your group or accept an invitation. I'm not snooty--I'm just up to my eyeballs in work and appearances!<br /><br />Also, don't be alarmed by the number of books I've read. When I get bored, I go through the different lists and rediscover books I've read in the past. It's a very evil way to use up time when I should be doing other things. Obviously, I've read a lot of books in 54 years!<br /><br />I was born in South Connellsville, PA. My mother wanted to name me "Tamara" but the nurse who filled out my birth certificate misspelled it as "Tamora". When I was 8 my family moved to California, where we lived for 6 years on both sides of the San Francisco peninsula.<br /><br />I started writing stories in 6th grade. My interest in fantasy and science fiction began when I was introduced to ‘The Lord of the Rings’ by J. R. R. Tolkien and so I started to write the kind of books that I was reading. After my parents divorced, my mother took my sisters and me back to Pennsylvania in 1969. There I went to Albert Gallatin Senior High for 2 years and Uniontown Area Senior High School for my senior year.<br /><br />After graduating from the University of Pennsylvania, I wrote the book that became The Song of the Lioness fantasy quartet. I sold some articles and 2 short stories and wrote reviews for a martial arts movie magazine. At last the first book of the quartet, Alanna: The First Adventure was published by Atheneum Books in 1983.<br /><br />Tim Liebe, who became my Spouse-Creature, and I lived in New York City with assorted cats and two parakeets from 1982 - 2006. In 2006 we moved to Syracuse, New York, where we live now with assorted cats, a number of squirrels, birds, raccoons, skunks, opossums, and woodchucks visiting our very small yard. As of 2011, I have 27 novels in print, one short story collection, one comic book arc ("White Tiger: A Hero's Compulsion") co-written with Tim, and a short story anthology co-editing credit. There's more to come, including a companion book to the Tortall `verse. So stay tuned!</span>
